    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

  <span id="freeText18379368036077755014" style="display:none">Want to Help Your Kids Win Friends? Terry Treetop Animation #1 Best seller in Children's Action &amp; Adventure Books ! (Animal Habitats &amp; Environment children's books collection) This is a wonderful book about a boy named Terry, but everybody calls him Terry Treetop because he loves climbing trees. Terry was alone, so he went on a journey to find new friends to invite to his new tree house. He almost gives up when a new opportunity comes his way. Will Terry use this opportunity to find new friends? This beginner readers eBook series will motivate and inspire your kids to be active about the things they want to achieve in life and not give up on their quest for love and happiness. Your kids will enjoy full-color illustrations of Terry and the farm animals he meets. Your kids will be inspired to: Be self-motivated Persist and not give up Win new friends Terry Treetop Finds New Friends is a sweet children's book written especially for you and your age 2- 6 children with simple text and 16 colorful illustrations. The story is suitable as a read aloud book for preschoolers or a self-read book for beginner readers children.</span>

  <span id="freeText6081024964161987453" style="display:none">This is a sweet book about finding new friends - Terry has a new tree house and now he wants to find friends to share the fun with him - He meets lots of new animal friends along the way and even if they can't come right now he is happy as he progresses on his journey to find friends that can play now - he even helps one in the end.<br /><br />I like the illustrations and the bright colors - I think this is a great book for kids to read with their parents - new friends are hard to find some days but Terry makes the best of it - I would have liked him to meet some human friends also to share his tree house with - if your child loves to be read too or with this is a sweet book to try.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1059060185" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer417444551306817393">I was given the opportunity to review this book and so I downloaded it for my 3 boys ages 9, 7 & 3. The 3 year old loved it and I am sure we will be reading this book many times. My other two found it entertaining as well.<br/><br/>I liked that the illustrations are cute, bright and colorful. The colors really popped on the kindle. This is such a sweet and happy story about a little boy looking for friends. It teaches that sometimes making friends is not easy, but to never to give up. It becomes education</span>
  <span id="freeText417444551306817393" style="display:none">I was given the opportunity to review this book and so I downloaded it for my 3 boys ages 9, 7 &amp; 3. The 3 year old loved it and I am sure we will be reading this book many times. My other two found it entertaining as well.<br /><br />I liked that the illustrations are cute, bright and colorful. The colors really popped on the kindle. This is such a sweet and happy story about a little boy looking for friends. It teaches that sometimes making friends is not easy, but to never to give up. It becomes educational along Terry’s journey to find a friend when the animals he meets are all busy doing something important, such as: “Betty the Bee” was busy filling jars with honey and couldn’t play. My 3 year old wanted to know why the bee was filling jars with honey, and I explained that bees are where we get honey from. I liked that every animal that Terry meets teach the listeners of the story the importance of what they do in their “life”. Of course, the cutest animal I thought was “Kitty”, who was crying and stuck in a treetop. Terry is the best tree climber (hence the name) and so rescues Kitty.<br /><br />I received one or more of the products mentioned above for free using Tomoson.com. Regardless, I only recommend products or services I use personally and believe will be good for my readers.</span>

<div id="review_1058558102" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1058558102" />
    <a title="Kathy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1143268-kathy"><img alt="Kathy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1493572653p2/1143268.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1058558102?book_show_action=true">Sep 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathy" href="/user/show/1143268-kathy">Kathy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1058558102" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2367982002560335265">I love the pictures in this children's storybook. They are bright and colorful and I like Terry's patched up pants and shirt. This is a cute story book and the text flows easily when read aloud. Terry does a heroic deed at the end winning him the friends he has been seeking.<br/><br/>The only reason I liked this book instead "loving" it was I thought that Terry could have made more of an effort from the very beginning to be a friend. He passes all these animals who are hard at work hoping one of them will</span>
  <span id="freeText2367982002560335265" style="display:none">I love the pictures in this children's storybook. They are bright and colorful and I like Terry's patched up pants and shirt. This is a cute story book and the text flows easily when read aloud. Terry does a heroic deed at the end winning him the friends he has been seeking.<br /><br />The only reason I liked this book instead "loving" it was I thought that Terry could have made more of an effort from the very beginning to be a friend. He passes all these animals who are hard at work hoping one of them will come to his new tree house to play. Not once does he offer to help them which seemed like the logical way to make a new friend.<br /><br />When reading picture books I prefer to have pictures on the screen at all times to hold children's interest. All the pictures in this story are square and then the text appears below the picture. This works fine when there is limited text but there are several times when the amount of text if too long so it flows onto the next page leaving only a bunch of text to be read.<br /><br />I received a review copy of this book in exchange for an honest review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2367982002560335265" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Sims" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Sims" href="/user/show/34297991-sarah-sims">Sarah Sims</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1061598583" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7680218780990444264">Terry Treetop is a special character. He is one that kids easily relate to and form a bond with. In some ways he reminds me of Dora the Explorer, but without the backpack. Terry decides what he wants to do and goes out to find the best way to accomplish this task. In Terry Treetop Finds New Friends, Terry is so excited to have a new tree house! He finds that his tree house is lonely by himself, however, and he goes off to look for someone special to share it with.<br/><br/>His journey to find someone to s</span>
  <span id="freeText7680218780990444264" style="display:none">Terry Treetop is a special character. He is one that kids easily relate to and form a bond with. In some ways he reminds me of Dora the Explorer, but without the backpack. Terry decides what he wants to do and goes out to find the best way to accomplish this task. In Terry Treetop Finds New Friends, Terry is so excited to have a new tree house! He finds that his tree house is lonely by himself, however, and he goes off to look for someone special to share it with.<br /><br />His journey to find someone to share his tree house with taught him and his friends some valuable social lessons. The lessons learned in the Terry Treetop books are exactly the reason I keep coming back to these books. A good book that teaches social skill lessons in a way that preschool and kindergarten age children understand is a real gem in today's children's book market. Any story is only useful and good if the children are excited by it and willing to listen to it. My 4 year old loves to listen to Terry Treetop's adventures and my 5 year old (he turns 6 this week!!) is using Terry Treetop to learn to read!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7680218780990444264" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Betty the Bee, Shelly the Sheep, Cherry the Chicken, and Kelly the Cow) he meets are all too busy to be Terry's friend and he continues searching for someone. Terry finally decides to hea</span>
  <span id="freeText797911820182937723" style="display:none">A cute story about Terry Treetop and the friends and values he meets along his adventures. It is a cute story and has wonderful, vivid illustrations! The story is written for children around the ages 3-8.<br /><br />The story follows Terry throughout a journey as he searches for a new friend. The animals (with great names! Betty the Bee, Shelly the Sheep, Cherry the Chicken, and Kelly the Cow) he meets are all too busy to be Terry's friend and he continues searching for someone. Terry finally decides to head home and finds a kitten stuck in a tree. Finally a friend! Terry uses his fantastic skill of climbing trees to reach the Kitty and save him! All of the characters go back to his treehouse<br /><br /> The illustrations were very well done, bright, and engaging. They helped to tell the story along with the words, which helps drawn the younger readers/listeners into the story.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6839990348081297355">I was delighted by Terry Treetops Finds New Friends by Tali Carmi. Written for Children 2 years - 6 years old, there are several opportunities for parent child/discussion. Terry Treetops loves climbing trees and his dad picks Terry's favorite tree to build a treehouse for him. It isn't very long before Terry realizes that his treehouse would be much more fun if he had a friend to enjoy it with. He decides to go on a journey to find a friend and meets several well illustrated animals. However, ea</span>
  <span id="freeText6839990348081297355" style="display:none">I was delighted by Terry Treetops Finds New Friends by Tali Carmi. Written for Children 2 years - 6 years old, there are several opportunities for parent child/discussion. Terry Treetops loves climbing trees and his dad picks Terry's favorite tree to build a treehouse for him. It isn't very long before Terry realizes that his treehouse would be much more fun if he had a friend to enjoy it with. He decides to go on a journey to find a friend and meets several well illustrated animals. However, each one is too busy to go back with Terry Treetops to play. Instead of helping his new friend with his work, he chooses to go on his way, missing a chance to be a good friend. In the end, Terry learns an important lesson about his strengths and about friendship. I highly recommend this book. </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1067068210" />
    <a title="Jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6015165-jessica"><img alt="Jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582815233p2/6015165.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1067068210?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica" href="/user/show/6015165-jessica">Jessica</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1067068210" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17017643981892294399">Rosalie wasn’t overly interested in looking at the pictures or listening to this book being read to her, because honestly, at 18 months old, I think she is a lot more interested in touching & turning the pages of a physical book! However, my boys enjoyed reading this book for their reading minutes that they have to do for school every day! <br/><br/>Michael did enjoy being able to read it to Rosalie, however, he was finished with it quite quickly. He’s a pretty advanced reader (4th-5th grade level and onl</span>
  <span id="freeText17017643981892294399" style="display:none">Rosalie wasn’t overly interested in looking at the pictures or listening to this book being read to her, because honestly, at 18 months old, I think she is a lot more interested in touching &amp; turning the pages of a physical book! However, my boys enjoyed reading this book for their reading minutes that they have to do for school every day! <br /><br />Michael did enjoy being able to read it to Rosalie, however, he was finished with it quite quickly. He’s a pretty advanced reader (4th-5th grade level and only in 2nd grade) so he always seems to gravitate towards chapter books already!<br /><br />Connor did enjoy it and he said that it taught him more about friendship than what he previously knew!<br />This is a good book to get, especially if you’ve got a 3-4 year old who enjoys being read to!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17017643981892294399" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17651756062826342101"><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://pebbleinthestillwaters.blogspot.com/2015/10/book-review-terry-treetop-finds-new.html'>http://pebbleinthestillwaters.blogspo...</a><br/><br/>Book Review: Terry Treetop Finds New Friends @tbcarmi Fabulous Cover and Story<br/><br/>Terry Treetop Finds New Friends carries a cheerful cover. Probably that is a good start to cheer up any kid who would be laying his hands on the book. And as we all know that every one of us has a kid inside irrespective of the age. So that way the book is good to lay hands on for anyone and everyone.<br/><br/>The cover has a cheerful Terry (the hero of the story) and a beautiful cat he is</span>
  <span id="freeText17651756062826342101" style="display:none"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://pebbleinthestillwaters.blogspot.com/2015/10/book-review-terry-treetop-finds-new.html">http://pebbleinthestillwaters.blogspo...</a><br /><br />Book Review: Terry Treetop Finds New Friends @tbcarmi Fabulous Cover and Story<br /><br />Terry Treetop Finds New Friends carries a cheerful cover. Probably that is a good start to cheer up any kid who would be laying his hands on the book. And as we all know that every one of us has a kid inside irrespective of the age. So that way the book is good to lay hands on for anyone and everyone.<br /><br />The cover has a cheerful Terry (the hero of the story) and a beautiful cat he is holding in his hands and touching cheek to cheek. The cat has a cute ribbon in her hair, wide beautiful and charming eyes; and a cute curly tail. The cat has cutely placed her one hand on Terry's arm and other on his cheek. The book has been written by Tali Carmi who is CEO of a software company but has a passion for writing for young kids. She was born in Israel. She is a proud veggie and has written over two dozen books mostly for young kids. Fabulous. The smiling Terry on the cover page is definitely going to bring a big smile on your face. The cheerful illustrations in the book are by Mindy Liang.<br /><br />Hang on. If you purchase this book you are automatically entitled to get a free gift - a great, fun and educational card game for you/ your kid. Is that not fantastic? Well, Terry has nothing to do with Treetop as far as his name is concerned. Treetop is added to his name because he is fond of climbing trees. Terry is a boy with red hair and bubbly cheeks always having a smile on his face and curiosity in his eyes. Curiosity to learn new things. Terry's dad is amazed at Terry's climbing trees passion and to add a new flavour to his adventure he builds a tree house for Terry on the top of his favourite tree in their backyard. Terry is delighted to get this new gift from his dad immediately climbs up the top of the tree to inspect his new house. Terry gets so amazed as he feels himself on the top of the world while looking down on the green fields from his new house.<br /><br />But the story takes a new turn immediately as Terry goes sad for a valid reason. To find out his genuine reason and what all he did to do away with this growing sadness you will have to grab the book and enjoy reading about his adventurous journey he took. On the way to his adventurous journey he finds many interesting friends. Terry Treetop Finds New Friends by Tali Carmi is really a fantastic read and a fabulous learning for young children (of any age)!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6278275115815694676"><br/>I have been trying to read a lot of children's books lately to inspire my own creative bug. To look at formatting "because I am self publishing with amazon here soon." and frankly to "selfishly force my babies to spend a little extra time with me" STORY TIME is a great excuse. <br/><br/> I came across this book "Terry Treetop finds new friends" Which is only one of a few in the series. At first, I was a little weary. I have bought probably 12 total children's books in kindle format and while I thought the</span>
  <span id="freeText6278275115815694676" style="display:none"><br />I have been trying to read a lot of children's books lately to inspire my own creative bug. To look at formatting "because I am self publishing with amazon here soon." and frankly to "selfishly force my babies to spend a little extra time with me" STORY TIME is a great excuse. <br /><br /> I came across this book "Terry Treetop finds new friends" Which is only one of a few in the series. At first, I was a little weary. I have bought probably 12 total children's books in kindle format and while I thought the stories were decent and the illustrations were good ... Avery was the toughest critic yet. <br /><br /> I figured. ONE DOLLAR. It's not a loss either way, it more than paid for itself in the moment I now get to cherish with my girls. <br /><br /> Avery has the attention span of a few seconds, sometimes minutes BUT FORGET anything in length needed for a full story. HOWEVER, that wasn't the case with this one. <br /><br /> She sat up strait and listened to every word ... Followed Terry treetop on his quest to find new friends the entire time. It's one of the sweetest little stories of a boy who loves to climb trees, who gets his dream tree house only to realize he needs a friend to share it with. In a world where everyone is busy and no one has time he finds a friend when he thinks hope is lost. A cute cuddly kitten stuck in a tree, which couldn't have been more perfect for the already lover of climbing trees terry. <br /><br /> It definitely teaches you that you can find friends by doing good deeds. Which is a moral that is great to instill in your children! We loved it. <br /> I will say that this book is more attractive to kids ages 2-7 It's an easy read. So if you are strapped for time and need a short story to appease your kids. This is a great one to start with. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9845524184272111717">My daughter and I love to read books and recently we have discovered Tali Carmi's series of books about Terry Treetop.   <span id="freeText9845524184272111717" style="display:none">My daughter and I love to read books and recently we have discovered Tali Carmi's series of books about Terry Treetop. When I was offered the chance to receive a digital copy of Terry Treetop Finds New Friends in exchange for an honest and unbiased review I couldn't refuse. We couldn't wait to see what new adventures Terry Treetop was going to go on.<br /><br />In Terry Treetop Finds New Friends Terry sets out to find some friends to play with him in his new tree house his dad has just built for him. Unfortunately everyone he asks to play is too busy working. But as Terry is walking home, sad and feeling lonely, he hears a cry from help. Kitty Kitten is stuck in a tree! Everyone runs to help but no one can climb a tree like Terry. Terry saves Kitty and then everyone heads over to Terry's tree house for a party. Now Terry is no longer alone.<br /><br />The illustrations are amazing. my daughter likes to just sit and go over all the details and talk about each picture before we flip to the next screen. The story is engaging for little ones. My daughter is almost 5 and she really enjoys the Terry Treetop stories. Even as an adult I enjoy them. Each story is filled with colorful pictures and stories that little ones love to hear.<br /><br />I would highly recommend this to the 1st grade and under crowd.<br /><br />I received a digital copy of Terry Treetop Finds New Friends complimentary for evaluation purposes.         <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1208186436" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7880027370123955007">The book features a cute little freckled boy named Terry that ventures forth to meet and befriend his animal neighbors. We follow Terry as he is turned away by the "hardworking" animals, but remains determined to find a friend. This book is not only a cute book with really great illustration, but also a children's book with a message. Terry keeps a positive attitude, even when the journey is tough.<br/>I did however, find flaw with the overall message. It seemed liked Terry should have offered to hel</span>
  <span id="freeText7880027370123955007" style="display:none">The book features a cute little freckled boy named Terry that ventures forth to meet and befriend his animal neighbors. We follow Terry as he is turned away by the "hardworking" animals, but remains determined to find a friend. This book is not only a cute book with really great illustration, but also a children's book with a message. Terry keeps a positive attitude, even when the journey is tough.<br />I did however, find flaw with the overall message. It seemed liked Terry should have offered to help his animal friends, instead of simply moving on. It's a small gripe, but it might have shown the value of putting a real effort into making a new friend. In the end Terry did make friends with all the animals.<br /><br />While my two year was not old enough to grasp the message of the book, he was really interested in the animals and their "jobs". The pictures were attractive to my little one, and he really enjoyed swiping through the pages to see all the animals. Included with this Ebook is a fun electronic card game that my son really enjoyed.<br /><br />* I received this product free in exchange for my unbiased review. I was not compensated for my review and all my opinions are my own. One may or may not have the same opinion as myself when reading this book. I am disclosing this in accordance with the Federal Trade Commission’s 16 CFR, Part 255: Guides Concerning the Use of Endorsements and Testimonials in Advertising. *</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8302204003852968981">"Terry Treetop Finds New Friends" by Tali Carmi is a story about a boy named Terry. Terry loved to climb trees so much, that everybody called him Terry Treetop! One day his dad built him a treehouse, where he could see forever, but he was sad when he realized he didn't have any friends who could play with him in his treehouse.<br/><br/>Terry went around to all the different farm animals, asking if they wanted to come and play in his treehouse, but one by one they all told him they had work to finish befor</span>
  <span id="freeText8302204003852968981" style="display:none">"Terry Treetop Finds New Friends" by Tali Carmi is a story about a boy named Terry. Terry loved to climb trees so much, that everybody called him Terry Treetop! One day his dad built him a treehouse, where he could see forever, but he was sad when he realized he didn't have any friends who could play with him in his treehouse.<br /><br />Terry went around to all the different farm animals, asking if they wanted to come and play in his treehouse, but one by one they all told him they had work to finish before they could play. Terry was so sad that he just decided to forget about finding a friend, and turned around to go home. Suddenly he heard someone calling for help! "Help! Help! Somebody help me!" Terry heard.<br /><br />All the other animals also heard the cry for help, but when they all gathered around the source of the cries, none of them could do anything to help. Only Terry was able to offer help and save the poor animal in distress. Soon all the animals wanted to play with Terry, and even had a picnic at his house, in honor of him saving the animal in distress.<br /><br />This is a cute story, and sure to be loved by many children. The illustrations are vividly colored, and the animals all are anthropomorphically cute, with big eyes and pleasant expressions. This story will be a popular addition to your child's book collection, and one I recommend heartily.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10053708864378262827">Terry Treetop is a great series and this book is no different. The reason I like this book and the Terry Treetop series is because Terry is independent and he believes that he can get what he wants. Terry finds his way home after chasing a butterfly and losing track of where he was, Terry helps a lost egg get home and even seeks help by climbing up a tree to view his surroundings in order to save a trapped dolphin in a fisher's net.<br/><br/>Terry is enjoying his tree house, but soon becomes lonely and go</span>
  <span id="freeText10053708864378262827" style="display:none">Terry Treetop is a great series and this book is no different. The reason I like this book and the Terry Treetop series is because Terry is independent and he believes that he can get what he wants. Terry finds his way home after chasing a butterfly and losing track of where he was, Terry helps a lost egg get home and even seeks help by climbing up a tree to view his surroundings in order to save a trapped dolphin in a fisher's net.<br /><br />Terry is enjoying his tree house, but soon becomes lonely and goes with a backpack and a peanut butter and jelly sandwich to find a new or new friends to bring back to his tree house. Terry encounters a large about of animals and some abnormally huge, but very charming and beautifully drawn. All the characters/animals can be seen doing something associated with what they do or are known for in real life, for example the Bee that Terry meets is storing honey to make buns and the sheep is heard clicking away while she knits.<br /><br />This book is takes about 12 minutes to read with out pause, 42 pages long and brightly illustrated. I would recommend it to children ages 4 or 5 to 8. My 8 year old and myself have read this book along with my 6 year old and have found it enjoyable and not complicated to understand. It is a good read out loud, read along, or independent book.<br /><br /><br />I received this book in exchange for an honest review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10053708864378262827" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer123833758574907665">This eBook features Terry Treetop, a little boy with red hair and freckles known for climbing trees. Terry goes on adventure to find new friends to play with him in his tree house but everyone he asks is too busy to play. If your child has ever felt lonely, they will certainly relate to this character and his feelings.<br/><br/>Since my children have special needs, they have restricted interests. Which means they don't always like characters they don't recognize. Unfortunately my children didn't really un</span>
  <span id="freeText123833758574907665" style="display:none">This eBook features Terry Treetop, a little boy with red hair and freckles known for climbing trees. Terry goes on adventure to find new friends to play with him in his tree house but everyone he asks is too busy to play. If your child has ever felt lonely, they will certainly relate to this character and his feelings.<br /><br />Since my children have special needs, they have restricted interests. Which means they don't always like characters they don't recognize. Unfortunately my children didn't really understand the story and showed little interest in this eBook. They did like the illustrations and I had them name the different animals that Terry Treetop met.<br /><br />In the end, Terry Treetop impresses everyone by saving the kitty that was stuck in the tree. Then all the people that were busy all have a party with Terry to celebrate that he saved the kitty from the tree. I am not certain why everyone is no longer busy but Terry Treetop is happy because he is not alone anymore.<br /><br />All in all, I think Terry Treetop is a lovable character that children can relate to. The story is cute and the beautiful illustrations bring the story to life.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5260056525453691957">Once again a Terry Treetop book Jasmine just loved. She loved all the pictures. She read the book herself and was able to tell me the moral right after. She is an 8 year old in the 3rd grade but struggles with reading and so every book she reads I reread it to her so she can better understand.<br/><br/>While she was reading it she stopped and said mom this is so sad, No one wants to go to Terry's tree house with him. I told her to keep reading that I bet one of those animals would come. So she kept going.</span>
  <span id="freeText5260056525453691957" style="display:none">Once again a Terry Treetop book Jasmine just loved. She loved all the pictures. She read the book herself and was able to tell me the moral right after. She is an 8 year old in the 3rd grade but struggles with reading and so every book she reads I reread it to her so she can better understand.<br /><br />While she was reading it she stopped and said mom this is so sad, No one wants to go to Terry's tree house with him. I told her to keep reading that I bet one of those animals would come. So she kept going. At the end I heard her say, "He did it, they all came and are having a party!"<br /><br />As a mom, I honestly love the lessons in these books. Never give up, keep trying! Be kind and people will be kind to you! I also love how there is a general moral but also little hidden lessons in the book. Like with the animals, this animals makes this food and that's how we get it, type lessons.<br /><br />You also get a free printable matching game that has to do with the characters in the book, which I thought was pretty cool. I didn't find it until after Jasmine had already went to bed but I'm sure will think its awesome.<br /><br />Overall this is a win-win for both mommy and Jasmine we both love Terry Treetop.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked

    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {

    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

Little Red’s granny lived a few miles down, near an old mill at the edge of town.  A wolf came by as she continued to walk, she didn’t know it was dangerous to talk. Red came knocking on the door: “Granny, are you better than before?”  “Come in, child. Red inched closer for a better look; and one glance was all it took.  “Granny, what big ears you’ve got; how could it have changed a lot?” “All the better to hear you Red, now come closer to my bed?”  “Granny, how big your eyes are too.” Red’s curiosity grew and grew. “All the better to see you Red, now come closer so I can kiss your head.”  “But Granny, your arms are big; and your hair looks like a funny wig. So changed and sharp are your teeth, it feels like you’re different underneath!”  “And so you are right little Red!” The wolf then sprang from the bed. Red gasped and tried to run; she looked for help but there was none!  A hunter came with a large knife; just in time to save Red’s life. He grabbed the wolf before it could bite, and cut of its head with all his might.  The wicked wolf was now dead, and in town the word had spread. Red was the safest she could be- and with kisses from mother and granny!  AND THE MORAL OF THIS STORY IS:   Don’t trust strangers right away. While not everyone will have bad intentions it is best to stay safe and be with people you know best. He spells out words and Minki picks out the letters from the set. She enjoys doing this except that she isn\'t able to tell p and q apart. So when Grandpa spells out p-i-g, she picks q, i, and g. For q-u-e-e-n she picks p,u,e,e,n and for q-u-i-l-t, she takes out the letters p,u,i,l,t.Because Minki has so much trouble with p and q, she throws them out of the window. Angry and hurt, p and q stomp away to Word Fairy and announce they are never going back.With p and q missing, many words become meaningless. Now nobody can say ‘please’ because it has turned into ‘lease.’ The police station and the post office can’t function and the queen must go into hiding!\n  \nWhich is p and Which is q? is a fun story about an important issue.\n  \n\n  Children between the ages 3 to 7 make occasional letter reversals while reading or writing. This is more likely to happen with letters that are mirror images of each other - like p and q, b and d, n and u. It doesn’t mean the child is dyslexic or has a learning ability. With practice and some clues, as the letter shapes become more familiar, children get over the confusion\n\n  .\nWhich is p and Which is q? is an engaging tale parents/ caregivers and children will enjoy. It teaches several things in an entertaining way:\n  1. How to make learning fun.\n\n  2. It is normal to make mistakes.\n\n  3. Children learn by practice.\n4. Actions have consequences : Minki\'s action makes p and q go away. Because p and q are miffed, words and sentences are in disarray!\n  5. One can learn from mistakes.\n\n  \nThis is an ‘anytime and for every one ’ story, suitable for playtime or bedtime, and one that girls and boys will both enjoy.  ***There is a FREE GIFT   <span id="freeText7945592547309709593" style="display:none">Tali Carmi spent her childhood in a small town in the desert.<br />She memorized and knew by heart many books that her parents read to her when she was very little. She played with words and rhymes and wrote her first book of songs at the age of ten.<br />After many years of turning to other hobbies and maintaining a successful career, she now writes again for young children.<br />Tali is the CEO and founder of a software company and a business coach focused on the fast growth and success of small businesses.<br />She holds a B.Sc. in Food Science and M.Sc.in Biotechnology, and she is a graduate of a Team Management and Leadership program.<br />Tali Carmi is happily married and a mom of three children.</span>
